                <tr id="so1" style="background-color: #FFF;"><td colspan="5" style="border-top:2px solid #D3D3D3; padding:3px; text-align:justify;"><div class="m_stories" style="width:100%; font-size:10pt"><center>Profiles:&nbsp;&nbsp;<a id="soa8" href="javascript:showMoreSO2016();">2016</a>&nbsp;&nbsp;(Click Year to Expand / <a href="javascript:hideSO('so1');">Close</a>)</center></div></td></tr>
                
                
                
                
                
                
                <tr id="so8" style="background-color: #FFF; display:none;"><td colspan="5" padding:3px; text-align:justify;"><div class="m_stories" style="font-size:10pt"><center><table><tr><td style="width:615px; padding-right:7px; text-align:justify;" valign="top"><b>Profile: </b>Castro was one of the players involved in the Troy Tulowitzki trade, and made a handful of appearances each for the Jays and Rockies. The 21-year-old was bad in Toronto, but worse in Colorado. I suspect Castro was promoted a bit over-aggressively last season. He hadn't thrown a pitch above High-A before last year, and also started 2015 at that level, before spending the rest of the season bouncing back and forth between Triple-A and the majors. (Scott Strandberg)<br /><br /><b>The Quick Opinion: </b>Castro has the stuff to be a force as a late-inning reliever someday, but he's very young and the command just isn't there yet. Expect him to start the season in Triple-A.</td></tr></table></center></div></td></tr>
